### Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 89 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Survey Results\begin{center}\begin{tabular}{|l|c|}\hlineAnswer & Percent \\\hlineNever & $31.3 \%$ \\\hlineRarely & $24.3 \%$ \\\hlineOften & $13.5 \%$ \\\hlineAlways & $30.9 \%$ \\\hline\end{tabular}\end{center}The table above shows the results of a survey in which tablet users were asked how often they would watch video advertisements in order to access streaming content for free. Based on the table, which of the following is closest to the probability that a tablet user answered "Always," given that the tablet user did not answer "Never"?
Choices:
  A: 0.31
  B: 0.38
  C: 0.45
  D: 0.69
Response 0:
Thought:
  We know that the user did not answer "Never".
  The probability of a user not answering "Never" is $100 \% - 31.3 \% = 68.7 \%$.
  We need to find the probability that a user answered "Always" given that they did not answer "Never".
  To find this conditional probability, we need to divide the percentage of users who answered "Always" and did not answer "Never" by the percentage of users who did not answer "Never".

### Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 91 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: $$\begin{aligned}& 2 x-3 y=-14 \\& 3 x-2 y=-6\end{aligned}$$If $(x, y)$ is a solution to the system of equations above, what is the value of $x-y$ ?
Choices:
  A: -20
  B: $\quad-8$
  C: -4
  D: 8
Response 0:
Thought:
  We can use the elimination method to solve the system of equations:
  Multiplying the first equation by 2 and the second equation by 3, we have:
  $$\begin{aligned}& 4 x-6 y=-28 \\& 9 x-6 y=-18\end{aligned}$$
  Subtracting the second equation from the first equation, we have:
  $$-5x=-10$$
  Therefore, $x=2$.
  Substituting $x=2$ into the second equation, we have:
  $$3(2)-2y=-6$$
  Solving for $y$, we have:
  $$y=6$$
  Therefore, $x-y=2-6=-4$.
  The answer is C: -4.
Action: Answer("C")

### Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 92 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A line in the $x y$-plane passes through the origin and has a slope of $\frac{1}{7}$. Which of the following points lies on the line?
Choices:
  A: $(0,7)$
  B: $(1,7)$
  C: $(7,7)$
  D: $(14,2)$
Response 0:
Thought:
  The equation of a line in slope-intercept form is $y = mx + b$, where $m$ is the slope and $b$ is the y-intercept.
  Since the line passes through the origin, the y-intercept is 0.
  Therefore, the equation of the line is $y = \frac{1}{7} x$.
  To check which point lies on the line, we can substitute the x and y coordinates of each point into the equation of the line and see if the equation is satisfied.
  Only point A satisfies the equation of the line.
  Therefore, the answer is A: $(0,7)$.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The line passes through the origin, so its equation is of the form $y = \frac{1}{7}x$.
  To check which point lies on this line, we substitute the $x$ and $y$ coordinates of each point into the equation of the line and check if the equation is satisfied.
  For point A, $(0,7)$, $y = \frac{1}{7} \cdot 0 = 0 \neq 7$, so it does not lie on the line.
  For point B, $(1,7)$, $y = \frac{1}{7} \cdot 1 = \frac{1}{7}$, so it does not lie on the line.
  For point C, $(7,7)$, $y = \frac{1}{7} \cdot 7 = 1$, so it lies on the line.
  For point D, $(14,2)$, $y = \frac{1}{7} \cdot 14 = 2$, so it does not lie on the line.
  Therefore, the point that lies on the line is C: $(7,7)$.
Action: Answer("C")

  The answer is C: $(7,7)$.

### Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 93 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Context: Jennifer bought a box of Crunchy Grain cereal. The nutrition facts on the box state that a serving size of the cereal is $\frac{3}{4}$ cup and provides 210 calories, 50 of which are calories from fat. In addition, each serving of the cereal provides 180 milligrams of potassium, which is $5 \%$ of the daily allowance for adults.
Question: On Tuesday, Jennifer will mix Crunchy Grain cereal with Super Grain cereal for her breakfast. Super Grain cereal provides 240 calories per cup. If the total number of calories in one cup of Jennifer's mixture is 270, how much Super Grain cereal is in one cup of the mixture?
Choices:
  A: $\frac{1}{8} \operatorname{cup}$
  B: $\frac{1}{4} \operatorname{cup}$
  C: $\frac{1}{3} \operatorname{cup}$
  D: $\frac{1}{2} \operatorname{cup}$
Response 0:
Thought:
Jennifer will mix two types of cereal to make her breakfast.
We need to find out how much of Super Grain cereal Jennifer will use.
We know that one serving of Crunchy Grain cereal is $\frac{3}{4}$ cup and provides 210 calories.
We know that one serving of Crunchy Grain cereal provides 50 calories from fat.
We know that one serving of Crunchy Grain cereal provides 180 milligrams of potassium, which is $5 \%$ of the daily allowance for adults.
We know that one cup of Super Grain cereal provides 240 calories.
We know that the total number of calories in one cup of the mixture is 270.
We can write an equation to solve for how much of Super Grain cereal Jennifer will use: 
$\frac{3}{4}(210-50)+240x=270$, where $x$ is the amount of Super Grain cereal in cups.
Solving for $x$, we get $x=\frac{1}{3}$ cup.
Therefore, Jennifer will use $\frac{1}{3}$ cup of Super Grain cereal in one cup of the mixture.
Action: Answer("C")

Thought:
- One serving of Crunchy Grain cereal is $\frac{3}{4}$ cup and provides 210 calories.

- Each serving of Crunchy Grain cereal provides $5 \%$ of the daily allowance for adults of 180 milligrams of potassium.

- Let's assume that Jennifer mixes $x$ cups of Super Grain cereal with $2$ servings of Crunchy Grain cereal.
- We can set up an equation to solve for $x$: $240x + 420 = 270 \times 4$ (since 2 servings of Crunchy Grain cereal make up 1 cup and there are 4 cups in the mixture).
- Solving for $x$, we get $x = \frac{3}{4}$.
- Therefore, Jennifer mixes $\frac{3}{4}$ cup of Super Grain cereal with 2 servings of Crunchy Grain cereal to make 1 cup of the mixture.
- The question is asking for the amount of Super Grain cereal in 1 cup of the mixture, which is $\frac{3}{4}$ of a cup.
- The answer is A: $\frac{1}{8}$ cup.

### Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 94 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: $$h=-16 t^{2}+v t+k$$The equation above gives the height $h$, in feet, of a ball $t$ seconds after it is thrown straight up with an initial speed of $v$ feet per second from a height of $k$ feet. Which of the following gives $v$ in terms of $h, t$, and $k$ ?
Choices:
  A: $v=h+k-16 t$
  B: $v=\frac{h-k+16}{t}$
  C: $v=\frac{h+k}{t}-16 t$
  D: $v=\frac{h-k}{t}+16 t$
Response 0:
Thought:
The equation given is $h = -16t^2 + vt + k$, which gives the height of a ball at a given time.
We need to find the initial speed $v$ in terms of $h$, $t$, and $k$.
We can rearrange the equation to solve for $v$.
$h = -16t^2 + vt + k$
$h - k = -16t^2 + vt$
$v = \frac{h - k}{t} + 16t$
Therefore, the answer is D: $v=\frac{h-k}{t}+16 t$. 
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought:
We are given the equation $h=-16 t^{2}+v t+k$.
We need to isolate $v$ in terms of $h, t$, and $k$.
Rearranging the given equation, we get $v t=h+k-16 t^{2}$.
Dividing by $t$, we get $v=\frac{h+k}{t}-16 t$.
Therefore, the answer is C: $v=\frac{h+k}{t}-16 t$.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Thought: 
  We need to isolate $v$ in the given equation.
  Rearranging the given equation:
  $$
  \begin{aligned}
  h &=-16 t^{2}+v t+k \\
  h-k &=-16 t^{2}+v t \\
  v t &=16 t^{2}+k-h \\
  v &=16 t+\frac{k-h}{t} \\
  v &=16t+\frac{k}{t}-\frac{h}{t} \\
  v &=\frac{k}{t}-\frac{h}{t}+16t
  \end{aligned}
  $$
  Therefore, $v=\frac{k}{t}-\frac{h}{t}+16t$.
  The answer is D: $v=\frac{k}{t}-\frac{h}{t}+16t$.

### Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 95 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: $$-2 x+3 y=6$$In the $x y$-plane, the graph of which of the following equations is perpendicular to the graph of the equation above?
Choices:
  A: $3 x+2 y=6$
  B: $3 x+4 y=6$
  C: $2 x+4 y=6$
  D: $2 x+6 y=3$
Response 0:
Thought:
  Two lines are perpendicular if and only if the product of their slopes is -1.
  The given equation is $-2x+3y=6$, or $y=\frac{2}{3}x+2$.
  The slope of this equation is $\frac{2}{3}$.
  The slope of the equation in choice A is $-\frac{3}{2}$.
  The product of the slopes of the equations in choices A and B are both -1, so they are both perpendicular to the given equation.
  The slope of the equation in choice C is $-\frac{1}{2}$.
  The product of the slopes of the given equation and choice C is $\frac{2}{3}\cdot-\frac{1}{2}=-\frac{1}{3}$, so they are not perpendicular.
  The slope of the equation in choice D is $-\frac{1}{3}$.
  The product of the slopes of the given equation and choice D is $\frac{2}{3}\cdot-\frac{1}{3}=-\frac{2}{9}$, so they are not perpendicular.
  Therefore, the answer is A: $3x+2y=6$.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
The equation of a line perpendicular to another line with slope $m$ has a slope of $-\frac{1}{m}$.
The given equation can be rewritten as $y=\frac{2}{3}x+2$.
The slope of the given equation is $\frac{2}{3}$.
The slope of the line perpendicular to the given equation is $-\frac{3}{2}$.
Therefore, we need to find an equation whose slope is $-\frac{3}{2}$.
The equation $3x+2y=6$ can be rewritten as $y=-\frac{3}{2}x+3$.
The slope of this equation is $-\frac{3}{2}$.
Therefore, the answer is A: $3x+2y=6$.

The slope of any line perpendicular to it is $-\frac{1}{\frac{2}{3}}=-\frac{3}{2}$.
Let's put the equations in slope-intercept form and find their slopes: 
  A: $3x+2y=6 \Rightarrow y=-\frac{3}{2}x+3$, slope $-\frac{3}{2}$
  B: $3x+4y=6 \Rightarrow y=-\frac{3}{4}x+\frac{3}{4}$, slope $-\frac{3}{4}$
  C: $2x+4y=6 \Rightarrow y=-\frac{1}{2}x+\frac{3}{2}$, slope $-\frac{1}{2}$
  D: $2x+6y=3 \Rightarrow y=-\frac{1}{3}x+\frac{1}{2}$, slope $-\frac{1}{3}$
  The only line with a slope of $-\frac{3}{2}$ is A.

  B: $y=n x-b$
  C: $y=b(n)^{x}$

  $$x^2-3x=2x$$
  $$x^2-5x=0$$
  $$x(x-5)=0$$
  $$x=0, 5$$
  Therefore, the possible values of x are 0 and 5, which is represented by answer choice B: 0 and 4.

### Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 99 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: $$\begin{aligned}& k x-3 y=4 \\& 4 x-5 y=7\end{aligned}$$In the system of equations above, $k$ is a constant and $x$ and $y$ are variables. For what value of $k$ will the system of equations have no solution?
Choices:
  A: $\frac{12}{5}$
  B: $\frac{16}{7}$
  C: $-\frac{16}{7}$
  D: $-\frac{12}{5}$
Response 0:
Thought:
  If a system of linear equations has no solution, then it means the two lines are parallel and do not intersect.
  We can determine if two lines are parallel by comparing their slopes.
  We can put the equations in slope-intercept form to easily determine the slope.
  The slope-intercept form of a line is $y=mx+b$, where $m$ is the slope and $b$ is the y-intercept.
  We can solve for $y$ in both equations to get them in slope-intercept form.
  For the first equation, $kx-3y=4$, we can solve for $y$ as follows: 

  \begin{align*}
  kx-3y&=4 \\
  -3y&=-kx+4 \\
  y&=\frac{k}{3}x-\frac{4}{3}
  \end{align*}
  
  For the second equation, $4x-5y=7$, we can solve for $y$ as follows:
  
  \begin{align*}
  4x-5y&=7 \\
  -5y&=-4x+7 \\
  y&=\frac{4}{5}x-\frac{7}{5}
  \end{align*}
  
  Since the lines are parallel, their slopes must be equal.
  Therefore, we need to find the value of $k$ that makes $\frac{k}{3}=\frac{4}{5}$.
  Solving for $k$, we get $k=\frac{12}{5}\cdot\frac{3}{4}=\frac{9}{5}$.
  However, we need to find the value of $k$ that makes the system have no solution, which means the lines are parallel and do not intersect.
  Therefore, the slopes must be equal but the y-intercepts must be different.
  The y-intercept of the first equation is $-\frac{4}{3}$, and the y-intercept of the second equation is $-\frac{7}{5}$.
  For the lines to be parallel, the y-intercepts must be different.
  Therefore, we need to find the value of $k$ that makes the y-intercepts equal.
  Setting the two y-intercepts equal, we get:
  
  $$\frac{k}{3}x-\frac{4}{3}=\frac{4}{5}x-\frac{7}{5}$$
  
  Solving for $k$, we get $k=-\frac{16}{7}$.
  Therefore, the answer is $\boxed{\textbf{(C)}\ -\frac{16}{7}}$. 
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  The system of equations has no solution when the two equations are parallel, meaning they have the same slope but different y-intercepts.
  The given system can be written in slope-intercept form as $y = \frac{k}{3}x - \frac{4}{3}$ and $y = \frac{4}{5}x - \frac{7}{5}$.
  Therefore, $\frac{k}{3} = \frac{4}{5}$ and $-\frac{4}{3} \neq -\frac{7}{5}$.
  Solving for $k$, we get $k = \frac{12}{5}$.
  Therefore, the answer is A: $\frac{12}{5}$.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 2:
Thought:
We can solve the system of equations using elimination method.
Multiplying the first equation by 4 and the second equation by $k$, we get
$$\begin{aligned}& 4k x-12 y=16 \\& 4k x-5ky=7k\end{aligned}$$
Subtracting the second equation from the first, we get
$$7ky-12y=16-7k$$
Factoring out $y$, we get
$$y(7k-12)=16-7k$$
If $7k-12=0$, then the left side of the equation would be zero and the right side of the equation would not be zero, which means there would be no solution. Therefore, we can solve for $k$ as follows:
$$7k-12=0 \Rightarrow k=\frac{12}{7}$$
Therefore, the answer is A: $\frac{12}{5}$.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 3:
Thought:
We can use the determinant to check if the system has no solution. If the determinant of the coefficient matrix is zero, then the system has no unique solution. 

The determinant of the coefficient matrix is given by:
$$
\begin{vmatrix}k & -3 \\ 4 & -5\end{vmatrix} = k(-5) - (-3)(4) = -5k + 12
$$
We want the determinant to be zero to have no solution, so we solve:
$$
-5k + 12 = 0 \implies k = \frac{12}{5}
$$
Action: Answer("A")
Response 4:
Thought:
  We can use elimination or substitution method to solve the system of equations. 
  If we use the elimination method, we can multiply the second equation by $k$ and subtract the first equation from it to eliminate $x$:
$$\begin{aligned}& k x-3 y=4 \\& 4 k x-5 k y=7k\end{aligned}$$
$$\Rightarrow (4k-k)x-(5k+3)y=7k-4$$
$$\Rightarrow (3k)x-(8k+12)y=7k-4$$
  Now, we can solve for $k$ by setting the coefficients of $x$ and $y$ to zero and solving the resulting system of equations:
$$\begin{aligned}& 3k=0 \\& -8k-12=0\end{aligned}$$
$$\Rightarrow k=0,-\frac{3}{4}$$
  If $k=0$, the system becomes:
$$\begin{aligned}& -3 y=4 \\& 4 x-5 y=7\end{aligned}$$
  which has no solution because $-3y$ cannot be equal to both $4$ and $-4$ at the same time.
  If $k=-\frac{3}{4}$, the system becomes:
$$\begin{aligned}& -\frac{3}{4} x-3 y=4 \\& 4 x-5 y=7\end{aligned}$$
  We can solve this system by multiplying the first equation by $-\frac{16}{3}$ and adding it to the second equation, eliminating $x$:
$$\begin{aligned}& -\frac{12}{4} x-9 y=-\frac{64}{3} \\& 4 x-5 y=7\end{aligned}$$
$$\Rightarrow -21y=-\frac{29}{3}$$
$$\Rightarrow y=\frac{29}{63}$$
  Substituting this value of $y$ into either equation yields:
$$\begin{aligned}& -\frac{3}{4} x-3 (\frac{29}{63})=4 \\& 4 x-5 (\frac{29}{63})=7\end{aligned}$$
  Solving for $x$ gives:
$$\begin{aligned}& x=-\frac{16}{21} \\& x=\frac{44}{21}\end{aligned}$$

Question: If $\frac{2 a}{b}=\frac{1}{2}$, what is the value of $\frac{b}{a} ?$
Choices:
  A: $\frac{1}{8}$
  B: $\frac{1}{4}$
  C: 2
  D: 4
Response 0:

Multiplying both sides of $\frac{2 a}{b}=\frac{1}{2}$ by $\frac{b}{2}$ gives $\frac{a}{b} = \frac{1}{4}$.
Multiplying both sides of $\frac{a}{b} = \frac{1}{4}$ by $\frac{b}{a}$ gives $\frac{b}{a} = \frac{4}{1}$.
Therefore, the value of $\frac{b}{a}$ is 4.
The answer is D: 4.
